    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer16563995988833302102">Three years ago, David Hunter moved to rural Norfolk to escape his life in London, his gritty work in forensics, and a tragedy that nearly destroyed him. Working as a simple country doctor, seeing his lost wife and daughter only in his dreams, David struggles to remain uninvolved when the corpse of a woman is found in the woods, a macabre sign from her killer decorating he</span>
  <span id="freeText16563995988833302102" style="display:none">Three years ago, David Hunter moved to rural Norfolk to escape his life in London, his gritty work in forensics, and a tragedy that nearly destroyed him. Working as a simple country doctor, seeing his lost wife and daughter only in his dreams, David struggles to remain uninvolved when the corpse of a woman is found in the woods, a macabre sign from her killer decorating her body. In one horrifying instant, the quiet summer countryside that had been David’s refuge has turned malevolent—and suddenly there is no place to hide.<br /><br />The village of Manham is tight-knit, far from the beaten path. As a newcomer, Dr. Hunter is immediately a suspect. Once an expert in analyzing human remains, he reluctantly joins the police investigation—and when another woman disappears, it soon becomes personal. Because this time she is someone David knows, someone who has managed to penetrate the icy barrier around his heart. With a killer’s bizarre and twisted methods screaming out to him, with a brooding countryside beset with suspicion, David can feel the darkness gathering around him. For as the clock ticks down on a young woman’s life, David must follow a macabre trail of clues—all the way to its final, horrifying conclusion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16563995988833302102" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1138232028" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1138232028?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>

          added it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1138232028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18303429891843631205"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436050759i/15412710._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Today I found my limit. Please don't laugh. <b>DNF because of <i>maggots</i></b>. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441920233ra/16168033.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>(I really wanted to add a maggot gif, but then I thought : googling that shit? Fuck no. Cats are safer)</i><br/><br/>See, I have a problem with maggots - and every fucking thing hovering around a dead body - I won't jump crying if I see <i>one</i>, but <i>plural</i>? I can't deal with this shit. Flies, larvae, chrysalis. <b>Welcome to my nightmare</b>. <br/><br/>No matter how good and compelling the writing is.<br/>No matter how daunting and oppressive the atmosphere is. <br/>None o</span>
  <span id="freeText18303429891843631205" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436050759i/15412710._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Today I found my limit. Please don't laugh. <b>DNF because of <i>maggots</i></b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441920233ra/16168033.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>(I really wanted to add a maggot gif, but then I thought : googling that shit? Fuck no. Cats are safer)</i><br><br>See, I have a problem with maggots - and every fucking thing hovering around a dead body - I won't jump crying if I see <i>one</i>, but <i>plural</i>? I can't deal with this shit. Flies, larvae, chrysalis. <b>Welcome to my nightmare</b>. <br><br>No matter how good and compelling the writing is.<br>No matter how daunting and oppressive the atmosphere is. <br>None of these exceptional qualities matter. <br><br>Because <i>maggots and flies</i>. <u>I. Can't. Deal. With. These. Descriptions</u>.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"The larvae here are mainly blowfly. Bluebottles and greenbottles. With the open wounds on the body we can expect insects to have been attracted straight away. They'll have started laying eggs within an hour if it was daylight.'<br>I poked about in the soil and picked up an unmoving maggot. I held it out on my palm. "This is about to pupate. The older they are the darker they get. By the look of this I'd say it was seven or eight days old. I can't see any husk fragments lying about, which mean no pupae have hatched yet."</b>
</blockquote><br>Apparently I'm okay (in love, I'd say) with serial killers and other dark shit but there's where I draw the line. Now, if you don't mind that kind of descriptions, I'm sure you'll find an incredible book here. Just not for me. Undoubtedly.<br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_38853691" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38853691" />
    <a title="Wendell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1756815-wendell"><img alt="Wendell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442473020p2/1756815.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38853691?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendell" href="/user/show/1756815-wendell">Wendell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780440335955" href="/book/show/1657060.The_Chemistry_of_Death">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1756815-wendell?shelf=trash-horror-guilty-pleasures">trash-horror-guilty-pleasures</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38853691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12228056890922712062">Given the unadulterated dreck that's so often foisted on fans of thriller/detective/murder mysteries - especially in the case of POD and self-published novels whose authors often have barely enough talent to write a check - *The Chemistry of Death* has one very important thing going for it: Beckett actually understands how to craft a decent English sentence. Unfortunately, two faults bog it down and keep it from being a star in the genre. First, no one has ever taught Beckett to murder his darli</span>
  <span id="freeText12228056890922712062" style="display:none">Given the unadulterated dreck that's so often foisted on fans of thriller/detective/murder mysteries - especially in the case of POD and self-published novels whose authors often have barely enough talent to write a check - *The Chemistry of Death* has one very important thing going for it: Beckett actually understands how to craft a decent English sentence. Unfortunately, two faults bog it down and keep it from being a star in the genre. First, no one has ever taught Beckett to murder his darlings, and no editor, whose job it would have been to have done so, evidently stepped in to fill the gap. That means that overwritten and purple passages crop up when you least expect them and are even more jarring because the rest of the writing is so clean. He's already got his hero copying Scarpetta's least proud moments with comments about how his job is to "make the dead tell their stories." Been there, slept through it. There's also the heavy-handed (heavy like a-teaspoonful-of-Pluto's-soil-weighs-a-squllion-tons-on-earth heavy) device of the protagonist's dreams, which are trite and soap-operaish and could have been cut without the slightest damage to the novel. Basically, dreams are a cheap, amateurish trick for revealing motivation or character; they can only mean one thing (exactly what the author tells you they mean) and, as such, they're a "cheat." If you want me to know something about the character, show it to me; don't make me sit through scenes in which the protagonist wakes up in a cold sweat trying to remember what's real and what's a dream and ... barf. In addition, *The Chemistry of Death* contains way (way) too many moments that remind one of another century's penny dreadfuls (the following are my inventions: "If I had only known what lay waiting for me in the garden, I would never have agreed to water Postman Abercrombie's prize-winning squash while he was away on holiday"; "As I watched the embers dying in the hearth, I could not have predicted that the next twenty-four hours would change the course of my life forever." That sort of thing. Ick. There's foreshadowing and then there's beating the reader over the head with the inkstand. Second, the "reveal" of this serial-killer mystery is such a hack job that it rather spoils what had been a great story up until then. It's literally one of those denouements in which, just as the hero finally confronts the killer in a life-or-death moment, the two of them stop and chat for 15 pages while the bad guy tediously explains why he did what he did and what everything meant and how he kept his crimes hidden and blah blah blah, revealing (in this case) a psychological motivation so superficial that you can feel Beckett grasping at straws to find an explanation that's halfway credible. And not quite getting there. That's a major problem: Beckett's the writer, he gets to choose which character to turn into a killer, and it's his job to make the reader believe it. Obviously, in every similar novel there's necessarily a moment in which the writer tells the reader whodunit, but Beckett wrote this ending with a rake. It's a shame, too, because the pacing of the book, which is rather leisurely at times, is betrayed by this paint-by-numbers ending. All in all, a good effort and an enjoyable read with several irritating flaws.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12228056890922712062" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=uk-author-setting">uk-author-setting</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48372551-li-l-owl?shelf=detective-police-procedural-sheriff">detective-police-procedural-sheriff</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1782746850" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14312025634276284071">Three years ago Dr. David Hunter left London leaving behind the city, his job as a forensic pathologist, and the tragedy of losing his wife and daughter in a fatal car accident. Now he works alongside his partner Dr. Henry Maitland as a local GP in the rural village of Manham, Norfolk, his life is simple and quiet. <br/><br/>Then on a scorchingly hot summer in July 11 year old Niel and his younger brother Sam, age 8, were headed to the local pond to for some relief from the searing sun and heat when they </span>
  <span id="freeText14312025634276284071" style="display:none">Three years ago Dr. David Hunter left London leaving behind the city, his job as a forensic pathologist, and the tragedy of losing his wife and daughter in a fatal car accident. Now he works alongside his partner Dr. Henry Maitland as a local GP in the rural village of Manham, Norfolk, his life is simple and quiet. <br /><br />Then on a scorchingly hot summer in July 11 year old Niel and his younger brother Sam, age 8, were headed to the local pond to for some relief from the searing sun and heat when they came across a dead body in the woods. David is called out to visit the Yates home shortly after as the boys, Sam in particular is badly shaken by the discovery. <br /><br />Local chief inspector Mackenzie asks David for help in determing time of death. David puts him off, wanting nothing to do with the case but Mackenzie wasn't done trying to persuade David into helping. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>'"You won't change your mind?"<br /> I've told you as much as I can."<br />"You could tell us more if you wanted to." <br /><br />Feeling angry by the way he was trying to manipulate me I told him I'd done what he had asked. <br />Detective Mackenzie seemed to be weighing something up as he squinted into the sun. <br /><br />"The Situation's changed." He said reaching a decision. "Somebody else has gone missing. You might know her."<br /><br />With that he turned and walked away his shadow chasing him across the grass like a black dog at his heels.'</b>
</i><br /><br />With that, David finds he has no choice to help, finding himself caught up in the investigation alongside Mackenzie hoping his past forensic knowledge can prevent the loss of another innocent life. <br /><br />But getting involved in the case also catches him between the police and the villagers as even after three years, Dr. David Hunter is still considered an outsider which makes him a suspect in the murder in the eyes of the village locals. <br /><br />The case takes on a nightmarish quality when they discover that the killer is leaving gruesome and macabre clues surrounding the murder and the missing woman and Chief Mackenzie and Dr. David Hunter are in a race against time to put the pieces together before the killer completes his next shocking murder. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46465.The_Chemistry_of_Death__David_Hunter___1_" title="The Chemistry of Death (David Hunter, #1) by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Chemistry of Death</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26024.Simon_Beckett" title="Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">Simon Beckett</a> is a chilling and edgy thriller with true crime forensic pathology at it's best. I loved all the detailed characters and the descriptive writing leaves nothing to the imagination. There's no time for a breather as the pages fly by at a frienzed pace. If time had permitted I would have read this in one sitting! This is the first of the <i>David Hunter</i> series and it came out of the gate at a full gallop! I can't wait to read the next book in this exciting series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6499985.Written_in_Bone__David_Hunter__2_" title="Written in Bone (David Hunter #2) by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">Written in Bone</a>. <br /><br />If you like the <i>Body Farm</i> series by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2747568.Jefferson_Bass" title="Jefferson Bass" rel="nofollow noopener">Jefferson Bass</a> you'll definitely love this series! <br />Highly recommended!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14312025634276284071" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/885832355" />
    <a title="Tim The Enchanter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5654692-tim-the-enchanter"><img alt="Tim The Enchanter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386188040p2/5654692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/885832355?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim The Enchanter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim The Enchanter" href="/user/show/5654692-tim-the-enchanter">Tim The Enchanter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6502865-the-chemistry-of-death">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=my-ebooks">my-ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer885832355" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11860837495754750870">This is another of my vacation reads that I am finally getting around to reviewing.<br/><br/><b>
  <u> Saved by a big Finish - 2 Stars </u>
</b><br/><br/>It has taken me a while to get around to reviewing this one. The main reason is that I have been trying to think of something interesting to say about my experience. Problem is, there is not much interesting content to discuss. <br/><br/><b> The Plot </b><br/><br/>In this story we have David Hunter, a forensic anthropologist who tries to escape a painful past by taking the position of a small town family</span>
  <span id="freeText11860837495754750870" style="display:none">This is another of my vacation reads that I am finally getting around to reviewing.<br /><br /><b>
  <u> Saved by a big Finish - 2 Stars </u>
</b><br /><br />It has taken me a while to get around to reviewing this one. The main reason is that I have been trying to think of something interesting to say about my experience. Problem is, there is not much interesting content to discuss. <br /><br /><b> The Plot </b><br /><br />In this story we have David Hunter, a forensic anthropologist who tries to escape a painful past by taking the position of a small town family doctor. He is assisting with the practice of the town's long-time resident doctor, who is struggling with his practice after becoming wheelchair bound after an accident. David's retreat in the countryside is successful for a few year until a dead and bloated body is found in the woods. David's is forced to fight the demons of his past as he is reluctantly thrust back into a trade he has all but abandoned.<br /><br /><b> The Bad </b><br /><br /><u> Can we Start this Again...</u><br /><br />Flat. This is the word that best describes the characters. The MC was depressed and hiding and it felt like he was dragging himself around and the story down with him. The secondary characters were underdeveloped.<br /><br />Contrived. The word that best describes the plot. The manner in which the MC was dragged back into forensic anthropology was poorly executed. Here we have one of the best (and few) forensic anthropologist in the UK who happens to keep this as a secret while moving to a small town where bodies start to pile up. Additionally, the ending, although quite exciting caused me to role my eyes. The author didn't build the story to the eventual ending and dropped a bunch of "Betcha you didn't see that coming" surprises on the reader. Even though I felt a bit cheated at the end...<br /><br /><b> The Good </b><br /><br /><u> At Least We Will Always Have the Ending </u><br /><br />Yes, the ending did piss me off a bit. Once I got over my frustration, it turned out the ending was the best written and most interesting part of the book. Sure, there was forensics but it felt as if it was written by someone who read about it not someone who has used it in practice. The ending has some excellent confrontations, chases and poor decisions. It made a disappointing read a bearable read.<br /><br />I do not intend to read anymore of the series. The was very little in the book that I found to be redeeming and I simply do not care about the characters and do not care what will happen to them. <br /><br /><br /><br />Enjoyed the ending but almost quit a few times before I got there. Review after vaca. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11860837495754750870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText5555416152682637419" style="display:none">I liked this first book of the series a lot. The characters are interesting, as was the story. There was a little bit of a supernatural element having to do with dreams, that I could do without, but it wasn't a major part of the story.<br /><br />I had a feeling about the main villain, but rejected it, so I was surprised at how things turned out. There was another character that I thought might be the one, but unfortunately I was wrong - unfortunately because I wanted him to be the one.<br /><br />The small town where the action took place was not a very pleasant town. It seemed to have all the negatives of small towns without the positives. This is ignoring the fact that several murders took place there over the years. <div id="review_436113491" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/436113491" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/436113491?book_show_action=true">Oct 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer436113491" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7533138601287435025">Beckett takes the reader on a fabulous journey to the quaint English town of Manham, where tranquility appears to be the name of the game. With one General Practitioner, the town seems to be functioning fairly well, but a freak accident forces new blood to solve Manham's medical quandary. The arrival of a new doctor is not the only change in town, as dead animals and fowl begin to appear, coinciding with the new GP. When a body surfaces, our seemingly innocent GP reveals (to a select few) his se</span>
  <span id="freeText7533138601287435025" style="display:none">Beckett takes the reader on a fabulous journey to the quaint English town of Manham, where tranquility appears to be the name of the game. With one General Practitioner, the town seems to be functioning fairly well, but a freak accident forces new blood to solve Manham's medical quandary. The arrival of a new doctor is not the only change in town, as dead animals and fowl begin to appear, coinciding with the new GP. When a body surfaces, our seemingly innocent GP reveals (to a select few) his secret previous life as a forensic anthropologist in London. While keeping his surgery running as best he can, with an enfeebled partner, we see a new side to our friendly doctor. These bodies tell great tales about the time of death as well as the manner; something no back-water doctor would know. Using skills honed in London and Tennessee's Body Farm, the hunt is on for the murderer who must be hiding in plain sight. The victims pile up and when one close to the heart disappears, the manhunt kicks into high gear. The reader is left to evaluate who it might be behind all these grizzly murders: the butcher, the priest, the publican? With a culminating 30 pages that will leave the reader wondering where that plot line came from, Beckett weaves a masterful initial novel in this series, sure to bring the reader back for Round Two.<br /><br />With no prior history reading Beckett, I was pleasantly surprised at the book, especially since we are dealing with a journalist and not one who has or does work in the field. I felt small Jefferson Bass moments in the book, though the forensic anthropology was minimal. The story grows on you and the quaintness of the surroundings leaves the writer to wonder how anyone is such a lovely place could do anything so evil. I look forward to seeing what Beckett has in store in the rest of the series and will surely recommend this to anyone who likes the Reichs/Bass/Cornwell genre.<br /><br />Kudos, Mr. Beckett on a great opening to the series. Keep them coming!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7533138601287435025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Clay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6465921-clay"><img alt="Clay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361215303p2/6465921.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/273796832?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clay" href="/user/show/6465921-clay">Clay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6465921-clay?shelf=crime-noir-mystery">crime-noir-mystery</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer273796832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10637895198439624466">This used to be a bestseller. I am very sceptical about bestsellers, because they were written for the masses. And if it's written for everybody to understand, it's usually stupid, generic and predictable. But even though this books had many flaws I actually enjoyed it, because it was written really well. The idea, the setting and the characters were shallow to be honest, but the atmosphere of the book was its major quality. Whenever you opened the book, you could dive in into Manham, the place </span>
  <span id="freeText10637895198439624466" style="display:none">This used to be a bestseller. I am very sceptical about bestsellers, because they were written for the masses. And if it's written for everybody to understand, it's usually stupid, generic and predictable. But even though this books had many flaws I actually enjoyed it, because it was written really well. The idea, the setting and the characters were shallow to be honest, but the atmosphere of the book was its major quality. Whenever you opened the book, you could dive in into Manham, the place where the story takes place. It also drew some important influence from Arthur Miller's The Crucible which is another positive aspect.<br /><br />Now let me come back to the characters. When you think about it, could you really describe Dr. Hunter? What kind of character is he and how does he behave? In my opinion we don't even know that. He's such a flat character it's almost criminal. Even if you compare him to other characters from bestseller crime novels like Kurt Wallander he's nowhere on the same level. The girl he meets isn't a recognizable character either. I also didn't like the ending at all, it reminded me of a Hollywood script. Those last pages were awfully boring in my opinion. <br /><br />All in all the atmosphere of Manham and the great prose makes this book a very fast and easy read. Don't expect anything extraordinary, though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10637895198439624466" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_217661704" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/217661704" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4542979-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454402751p2/4542979.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/217661704?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/4542979-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4542979-kim?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4542979-kim?shelf=buddy-reads-with-jemidar">buddy-reads-with-jemidar</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer217661704" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1756221406342278580"><br/>The first in Beckett’s David Hunter series, this is a fast-paced thriller set in rural Norfolk. It tells the story of Dr David Hunter, who has left his career as a forensic anthropologist in London following a personal tragedy and works as a general practitioner in a small village. When the mutilated body of a local woman is discovered, he is reluctantly drawn into the police investigation. <br/><br/>This novel has some attractive features. Beckett can write decent prose, his grasp of the technicalities o</span>
  <span id="freeText1756221406342278580" style="display:none"><br />The first in Beckett’s David Hunter series, this is a fast-paced thriller set in rural Norfolk. It tells the story of Dr David Hunter, who has left his career as a forensic anthropologist in London following a personal tragedy and works as a general practitioner in a small village. When the mutilated body of a local woman is discovered, he is reluctantly drawn into the police investigation. <br /><br />This novel has some attractive features. Beckett can write decent prose, his grasp of the technicalities of forensic anthropology seems sound and there is no doubt that he has written a page-turner with some unpredictable twists. In addition, Hunter is a well-drawn and sympathetic protagonist.<br /><br />However, the book does have a number of problems. Probably the most significant of these is that Beckett overuses foreshadowing. There are way too many instances of Hunter (who is the first person narrator for most of the novel) saying things such as “I didn’t know it then, but that was about to be proved in the way I least expected” and “In the coming days I would look back on this afternoon as one last glimmer of blue sky before the storm” with monotonous regularity. That sort of thing may be okay once or twice, but it soon got to be seriously annoying. Another problem is the use of gothic elements – particularly dreams – which don’t really add anything to the narrative. <br /><br />Other problems may have more to do with me than they do with the book. Maybe in the past I read too much <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1025097.Patricia_Cornwell" title="Patricia Cornwell" rel="nofollow noopener">Patricia Cornwell</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26372.Kathy_Reichs" title="Kathy Reichs" rel="nofollow noopener">Kathy Reichs</a>* and watched one season too many of <i>Silent Witness</i>, or maybe it’s just that I’ve become more squeamish with age, but I find it increasingly difficult to read weird serial murderer stories. In particular, I find it very difficult to read about women being abducted and tortured, which is a feature of the novel. I also find it difficult to read about the mistreatment of animals and - not to put too fine a point on it - there are quite a lot of dead animals in this novel. I could say that the implausibility of the plot is another weakness of the novel. There’s no doubt that it is stunningly implausible, but implausibility goes with the territory of the crime fiction genre. Readers who need a believable narrative should probably avoid the genre altogether. That said, a slightly more persuasive ending would have been welcome.<br /><br />This is not a bad effort for a first novel and I’ll read the second novel in the series before I decide if I want to read any more. If Beckett keeps writing overly gruesome serial murderer stories laced with heavy-handed foreshadowing, then that may be the end of the road for me. But I’m glad to have given a new series a try and, as always, I’ve really enjoyed the buddy read with my good friend Jemidar. For me, the book rates in the region of 3-1/2 stars, mostly because it really is a page-turner. I’d like to have been able to rate it more highly, but in recent times I’ve given four stars to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10015.Kate_Atkinson" title="Kate Atkinson" rel="nofollow noopener">Kate Atkinson</a>’s novels and in my view Beckett is nowhere near as accomplished a writer. <br /><br />*It's been quite some time since I read either of these authors. Cornwell I started to dislike after her first few books and Reichs I gave up reading because of the way she deals with the interpersonal relationships of her main character. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1756221406342278580" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1219527520" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1219527520" />
    <a title="Jaksen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7233842-jaksen"><img alt="Jaksen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455934399p2/7233842.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1219527520?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaksen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaksen" href="/user/show/7233842-jaksen">Jaksen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1219527520" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16616182049318213572">Took me two days to read this! Yes, and it wasn't the only thing I did! <br/><br/>The story of a young doctor gone to live and work in rural England following the death of his wife and child. Yeah, a trope, but it's always in the <i> way </i> a writer handles a trope that defines a book. (If not for tropes we'd have no mysteries at all, romance would be nil, and no little boys would be going off to boarding schools and learn about monsters, magic and those-who-must-not-be-named.) Anyhow, this doctor, David Hunte</span>
  <span id="freeText16616182049318213572" style="display:none">Took me two days to read this! Yes, and it wasn't the only thing I did! <br /><br />The story of a young doctor gone to live and work in rural England following the death of his wife and child. Yeah, a trope, but it's always in the <i> way </i> a writer handles a trope that defines a book. (If not for tropes we'd have no mysteries at all, romance would be nil, and no little boys would be going off to boarding schools and learn about monsters, magic and those-who-must-not-be-named.) Anyhow, this doctor, David Hunter, wants to stick close to home base, make a few house calls, be available for 'surgery,' - or doctor's hours - and just lay low. He's a bit depressed, a lot unhappy, and of course...<br /><br />There's a murder! A body found in a woods with swan wings jutting out of her back! This is no spoiler, it happens very early on. Of course, Dr. Hunter doesn't want to get involved or let on to local law enforcement that ummm, hey I was a forensic anthropologist before I decided to be an ordinary physician. So, just leave me alone, okay?<br /><br />No, of course not. As Dr. Hunter is unwillingly drawn into a complex murder investigation that rapidly expands...<br /><br />Well that would be going into spoiler territory. Suffice to say this is a fast book, but a good one. Enough description to put you smack into the middle of marshes and shallow lakes; dialogue that rings true to the ear - people really talk like this! - and a story that's intriguing enough to make you think about it as you walk away. Plus possible suspects? Please, there's a dozen of them!<br /><br />I loved this book, will read more by Mr. Beckett for sure.<br /><br />Four stars, or maybe a 4.5. Loved it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16616182049318213572" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1784030364" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1784030364" />
    <a title="Cleopatra  Pullen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3162627-cleopatra-pullen"><img alt="Cleopatra  Pullen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466403301p2/3162627.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1784030364?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cleopatra  Pullen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cleopatra  Pullen" href="/user/show/3162627-cleopatra-pullen">Cleopatra  Pullen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3162627-cleopatra-pullen?shelf=2016-favourites">2016-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3162627-cleopatra-pullen?shelf=crime-series">crime-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3162627-cleopatra-pullen?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3162627-cleopatra-pullen?shelf=crime">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1784030364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2515793673616848994">Following the tragic death of his wife and daughter David Hunter lands in a remote village of Manham in Norfolk as a partner to the resident doctor. The villagers are, as those in tight-knit communities tend to be, slow to take to him and still prefer Doctor Henry Maitland to tend to their ills, despite the fact that he has been badly disabled by a car accident. The two doctors initially share the house as well as the surgery but as David Hunter is slowly tolerated, if not accepted, he decides t</span>
  <span id="freeText2515793673616848994" style="display:none">Following the tragic death of his wife and daughter David Hunter lands in a remote village of Manham in Norfolk as a partner to the resident doctor. The villagers are, as those in tight-knit communities tend to be, slow to take to him and still prefer Doctor Henry Maitland to tend to their ills, despite the fact that he has been badly disabled by a car accident. The two doctors initially share the house as well as the surgery but as David Hunter is slowly tolerated, if not accepted, he decides to put down roots and moves to a nearby house. All is going tolerably well, he drinks in the local pub and makes light conversation with some of the locals and is even invited to a barbeque until the body of a woman is found in the woods. The outsiders are under suspicion!<br /><br />What the locals don’t know is that Dr David Hunter is a forensic anthropologist who has actually visited the body farm in the US – something I learnt about in for the first time through another crime fiction novel. When the police talk to him regarding their suspicions about his past he is forced to reveal that he is one of the few in the country. It isn’t long before he is asked to carry out his specialism on the crime committed, something our protagonist is keen to avoid having shunned the limelight and the associated dead bodies following the tragedy in his personal life.<br /><br />Soon more bodies are found but The Chemistry of Death somehow raises the bar beyond the horrors of the crimes committed, although I don’t recommend this for the squeamish, because of the exceptional quality of the writing by the author. Not only is this superbly plotted with a classic whodunit at the heart of the novel, the prose seems to effortlessly conjure up the village, its inhabitants and their interactions. It is soon clear everything is not as it first appeared and not only does Simon Beckett throw in enough red herrings to keep the reader on their toes, he keeps it real and no major revelations made that don’t have the clues to back them up. A must in my opinion for a successful and more importantly satisfactory crime novel.<br /><br />With David Hunter providing the narration in his calm manner, by which I mean he fully captures the horror of the murders but still carries out his duties both as a doctor and a forensic anthropologist with exceptional care, we get his pitch perfect tone to walk us through the events as they unfold. What a joy to have a tale told in such a straightforward way with no writer’s ‘tricks’ to keep us on the edge of our seats, there is no need when the quality of the prose is as good as this is.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2515793673616848994" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5899772690143034967">Chemistry of Death of the first book in the Dr. David Hunter series. Hunter is a forensic expert who left his job in London after a tragedy forced him to make a change to his life. He's currently working in the small Norfolk village of Manham as a General Practitioner. While he can't stop dreaming of his dead family, he's as content as he can be under the circumstances. When the savagely mutilated body of Sally Palmer is found, Hunter knows he needs to help the police find the killer, despite hi</span>
  <span id="freeText5899772690143034967" style="display:none">Chemistry of Death of the first book in the Dr. David Hunter series. Hunter is a forensic expert who left his job in London after a tragedy forced him to make a change to his life. He's currently working in the small Norfolk village of Manham as a General Practitioner. While he can't stop dreaming of his dead family, he's as content as he can be under the circumstances. When the savagely mutilated body of Sally Palmer is found, Hunter knows he needs to help the police find the killer, despite his reluctance to return to his former profession. When another woman disappears, it becomes painfully clear that a serial killer is at work.<br /><br />I found this book quite gripping. It had a great story and the setting and characters were very realistic. The horrific details of what occurs to a decomposing body may not be for the faint of heart, but if you are a fan of Kathy Reichs and Patricia Cornwell you will really enjoy this book. I'm definitely planning to read the next in the series, Written in Bone.</span>

<div id="review_58771241" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/58771241" />
    <a title="Caitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2209914-caitlin"><img alt="Caitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1239417820p2/2209914.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/58771241?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caitlin" href="/user/show/2209914-caitlin">Caitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2209914-caitlin?shelf=2009">2009</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer58771241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9793130035374835089">I recently read Mr. Beckett's third book in this series, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4961571.Whispers_of_the_Dead' title='Whispers of the Dead by Simon Beckett' rel='nofollow noopener'>Whispers of the Dead</a>, & enjoyed it enormously which inspired me to go back & grab the first two.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46465.The_Chemistry_of_Death' title='The Chemistry of Death by Simon Beckett' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Chemistry of Death</a> is the first in the series starring David Hunter, British forensic anthropologist. I love books with forensic detail & these are right up my alley.<br/><br/>I love the fact that this book starts out with one of my favorite beginnings in literature: Our hero (or heroine), escaping from a tragedy & into a new life accepts a job in the</span>
  <span id="freeText9793130035374835089" style="display:none">I recently read Mr. Beckett's third book in this series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4961571.Whispers_of_the_Dead" title="Whispers of the Dead by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">Whispers of the Dead</a>, &amp; enjoyed it enormously which inspired me to go back &amp; grab the first two.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46465.The_Chemistry_of_Death" title="The Chemistry of Death by Simon Beckett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Chemistry of Death</a> is the first in the series starring David Hunter, British forensic anthropologist. I love books with forensic detail &amp; these are right up my alley.<br /><br />I love the fact that this book starts out with one of my favorite beginnings in literature: Our hero (or heroine), escaping from a tragedy &amp; into a new life accepts a job in the British countryside, sells all of his/her belongings, &amp; arrives by train in the distant village to begin their new life. Upon arrival said character is either picked up by odd retainer &amp; whisked away to the scary manor or finds themselves walking for miles into town because they haven't arranged a ride. It's a start you'll read in Delderfield's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/372853.To_Serve_Them_All_My_Days" title="To Serve Them All My Days by R.F. Delderfield" rel="nofollow noopener">To Serve Them All My Days</a> &amp; it's in my favorite Iris Murdoch novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11229.The_Sea__The_Sea__Penguin_Twentieth_Century_Classics_" title="The Sea, The Sea (Penguin Twentieth-Century Classics) by Iris Murdoch" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sea, The Sea</a>. It's got that touch of the gothic novel with windswept moors &amp; governesses &amp; strange new beginnings that I can't help but love, even when the book itself isn't all that great or even all that gothic.<br /><br />In this novel, Beckett plays with the English village mystery in setting, in happenings, in stock characters, &amp; in some plot details, but the form is morphed through a more modern forensic sensibility. It helps that Beckett writes clearly &amp; well, plots well, &amp; has a wonderful imagination. This was a thoroughly satisfying read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9793130035374835089" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

Their roles are limited to being victims and past/present love interests;<br/><br/>- the MC is depressed (because his wife and daughter are - guess what! - dead) and uses it as an excuse to be an a**hole but in the end he gets to play superhero.<br/><br/>I didn't really mind the maggots and flies - if I can't see them, they're not disgusting.   <span id="freeText561767296149303562" style="display:none">It's one of those books in which:<br /><br />- women get raped, kidnapped, tortured and murdered. Their roles are limited to being victims and past/present love interests;<br /><br />- the MC is depressed (because his wife and daughter are - guess what! - dead) and uses it as an excuse to be an a**hole but in the end he gets to play superhero.<br /><br />I didn't really mind the maggots and flies - if I can't see them, they're not disgusting. But it's just not a good novel. When the murderer was revealed my only reaction was laughter because it was so predictable and absurd. Honestly, it's the kind of a plot twist that happens in soap operas and while I was thinking that "hey, at least it'll be amusing if it happens" as I was reading the novel, when it actually did happen... My laughter bitter, not amused. </span>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780593055212" href="/book/show/1328722.The_Chemistry_of_Death">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=police_procedural">police_procedural</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=male_author">male_author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/250195-lj?shelf=contemporary_post_1945">contemporary_post_1945</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer4229742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18227002510167413783">THE CHEMISTRY OF DEATH (Suspense-Dr. David Hunter-England-Cont) – Okay<br/>Beckett, Simon – 1st book<br/>Bantam Press, 2006, UK Hardcover – ISBN: 0593055217<br/>First Sentence: A human body starts to decompose four minutes after death.<br/>*** Dr. David Hunter has come to a small town after answering an ad to assist in the practice of the town’s current GP. When the woman’s mutilated body is found, Hunter’s past is also found out. Hunter was once a high-profile forensic anthropologist. When another woman disappears</span>
  <span id="freeText18227002510167413783" style="display:none">THE CHEMISTRY OF DEATH (Suspense-Dr. David Hunter-England-Cont) – Okay<br />Beckett, Simon – 1st book<br />Bantam Press, 2006, UK Hardcover – ISBN: 0593055217<br />First Sentence: A human body starts to decompose four minutes after death.<br />*** Dr. David Hunter has come to a small town after answering an ad to assist in the practice of the town’s current GP. When the woman’s mutilated body is found, Hunter’s past is also found out. Hunter was once a high-profile forensic anthropologist. When another woman disappears, Hunter overcomes his hesitation to help the police but his secrecy leads the town to be suspicious. A third woman disappears; can Hunter find the killer in time to save her life?<br />*** This could have been a very good book, but it wasn’t. Where was this author’s editor? The story was peppered with “had I but known” portents that were distracting and did nothing to enhance or propel the story. The beginning reminded me of Jefferson Bass, but not as well done. I also had a problem with the common premise of the lead character still recovering from the loss of a loved one but fall in love almost immediately. There were some interesting characters in the story and, although it did move a bit slowly at times, that was offset by scenes with suspense so it wasn’t an awful book. Hopefully, the author will improve with his next book but I’ll wait to read it in paperback.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18227002510167413783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1689713305" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1689713305" />
    <a title="Pamela Mclaren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12623232-pamela-mclaren"><img alt="Pamela Mclaren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586956653p2/12623232.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1689713305?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pamela Mclaren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pamela Mclaren" href="/user/show/12623232-pamela-mclaren">Pamela Mclaren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780553817492" href="/book/show/1019896.The_Chemistry_of_Death">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12623232-pamela-mclaren?shelf=mysteries">mysteries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12623232-pamela-mclaren?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12623232-pamela-mclaren?shelf=from-janice">from-janice</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1689713305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12659822192366771214">I was hooked from the moment I began reading this book and was compelled to keep reading to the very end. It is that interesting a story.<br/><br/>David Hunter, a former forensic anthropologist fleeing London after the death of his wife and daughter in a DUI driving accident, arrives in the village of Manham and settles in as a partner in a medical practice with a doctor whose own wife had died in an accident. Everything seems to be fine until a body is found by two young boys. Slowly, police become aware</span>
  <span id="freeText12659822192366771214" style="display:none">I was hooked from the moment I began reading this book and was compelled to keep reading to the very end. It is that interesting a story.<br /><br />David Hunter, a former forensic anthropologist fleeing London after the death of his wife and daughter in a DUI driving accident, arrives in the village of Manham and settles in as a partner in a medical practice with a doctor whose own wife had died in an accident. Everything seems to be fine until a body is found by two young boys. Slowly, police become aware of Hunter's former career and expertise, but he continues to be desperate to remain uninvolved ... but by not being open about it, there is almost immediate suspicion by the villagers. <br /><br />Soon the ugliness of rumors bring out the worst in the villagers. While the police struggle to come up with suspects and clues to at the why, a dour religious leader decides to grab the spotlight and thing get even more tense and complex.<br /><br />And the complexity of this story, the complexity of the characters that makes it an ultimate must read. Definitely I'm hooked and I can't wait to read other books by this author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12659822192366771214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3agZX1NM841APlzqBaUO2OtF+4++YwFDSopqrV4xwABZBJYTpsuQHgloEQ6ULnRXDSVR3AOcMXMRTnOHjoGJCw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xMVPbDHBwoViYnKv3e2tg7eeBimtXvlZXnZRmutdDMVAacAgxEahFis0P0tMZtcMUf6sehChyWkFskiwO+1Fzg==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12028490963962528646">After an MA in English, Simon Beckett spent several years as a property repairer before a stint teaching in Spain. Back in the UK, he played percussion in several bands. He has been a freelance journalist since 1992, writing for The Times, The Independent on Sunday Review, The Daily Telegraph, The Observer and other major British publications. In 2002, as part of an article on the National Forensi</span>
  <span id="freeText12028490963962528646" style="display:none">After an MA in English, Simon Beckett spent several years as a property repairer before a stint teaching in Spain. Back in the UK, he played percussion in several bands. He has been a freelance journalist since 1992, writing for The Times, The Independent on Sunday Review, The Daily Telegraph, The Observer and other major British publications. In 2002, as part of an article on the National Forensic Academy, he visited the Body Farm in Tennessee. This last commission was the inspiration behind the internationally bestselling The Chemistry of Death, which was shortlisted for the CWA's Duncan Lawrie Dagger and has been translated into 21 languages. Simon Beckett is married and lives in Sheffield. The author of six novels, his second David Hunter thriller, Written in Bone, is published as a Bantam paperback in April 2008.</span>
